     <article class="devsite-article"> 
      <article class="devsite-article-inner"> 
       <nav class="devsite-breadcrumb-nav devsite-nav"> 
        <ul class="devsite-breadcrumb-list"> 
         <li class="devsite-breadcrumb-item"> <a href="https://firebase.google.com/" class="devsite-breadcrumb-link gc-analytics-event" data-category="Site-Wide Custom Events" data-label="Breadcrumbs" data-value="1"> Firebase </a> </li> 
         <li class="devsite-breadcrumb-item"> 
          <div class="devsite-breadcrumb-guillemet material-icons"></div> <a href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/" class="devsite-breadcrumb-link gc-analytics-event" data-category="Site-Wide Custom Events" data-label="Breadcrumbs" data-value="2"> Docs </a> </li> 
         <li class="devsite-breadcrumb-item"> 
          <div class="devsite-breadcrumb-guillemet material-icons"></div> <a href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/guides/" class="devsite-breadcrumb-link gc-analytics-event" data-category="Site-Wide Custom Events" data-label="Breadcrumbs" data-value="3"> Guides </a> </li>

       <nav class="devsite-page-nav-embedded devsite-nav"></nav> 
       <div class="devsite-article-body clearfix
            
              devsite-no-page-title
            " itemprop="articleBody"> 
        <span class="feature-intro-title"> <h1 itemprop="name" class="devsite-page-title devsite-page-title-with-icons"> <span class="heading-text">Firebase Cloud Messaging</span><span class="gmp-icons-container"><span class="gmp-platform-icons gmp-icon-ios material-icons" data-tooltip="iOS supported">plat_ios</span><span class="gmp-platform-icons gmp-icon-android material-icons" data-tooltip="Android supported">plat_android</span><span class="gmp-platform-icons gmp-icon-web material-icons" data-tooltip="Web supported">plat_web</span><span class="gmp-platform-icons gmp-icon-cpp material-icons" data-tooltip="C++ supported">plat_cpp</span><span class="gmp-platform-icons gmp-icon-unity material-icons" data-tooltip="Unity supported">plat_unity</span></span> </h1> </span> 
        <div class="feature-intro block"> 
         <p class="feature-intro tagline">Firebase Cloud Messaging (FCM) is a cross-platform messaging solution that lets you reliably deliver messages at no cost.</p> 
         <div class="video-wrapper"> 
          <iframe class="devsite-embedded-youtube-video" data-video-id="sioEY4tWmLI?list=PLl-K7zZEsYLmOF_07IayrTntevxtbUxDL" data-autohide="1" data-showinfo="0" frameborder="0" allowfullscreen> </iframe> 
         </div> Using FCM, you can notify a client app that new email or other data is available to sync. You can send notification messages to drive user reengagement and retention. For use cases such as instant messaging, a message can transfer a payload of up to 4KB to a client app.
         <p></p> 
         <p>Already using Google Cloud Messaging? <a href="https://firebase.google.com/support/faq/#gcm-fcm">Learn more</a> about your options.</p> 
         <p class="button-unindented"> <a class="button button-white button-lowercase" href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/ios/client">iOS SETUP</a> <a class="button button-white" href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/android/client">Android Setup</a> <a class="button button-white" href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/js/client">Web Setup</a> <a class="button button-white" href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/cpp/client">C++ Setup</a> <a class="button button-white" href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/unity/client">Unity Setup</a> </p> 
        </div> 
        <h2 id="key_capabilities">Key capabilities</h2> 
        <table class="responsive key-functions"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td>Send notification messages or data messages</td> 
           <td>Send notification messages that are displayed to your user. Or send data messages and determine completely what happens in your application code. See <a href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/concept-options.html#notifications_and_data_messages"> Message types</a>.</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td>Versatile message targeting</td> 
           <td>Distribute messages to your client app in any of three ways  to single devices, to groups of devices, or to devices subscribed to topics. </td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td>Send messages from client apps</td> 
           <td>Send acknowledgments, chats, and other messages from devices back to your server over FCMs reliable and battery-efficient connection channel.</td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
        <h2 id="how_does_it_work">How does it work?</h2> 
        <div class="clearfix"> 
         <img src="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/images/messaging-overview.png" alt="Firebase Cloud Messaging architecture diagram" class="attempt-right"> 
         <p>An FCM implementation includes two main components for sending and receiving: </p>
         <ol>
          <li>A trusted environment such as Cloud Functions for Firebase or an app server on which to build, target and send messages.</li> 
          <li>An iOS, Android, or Web (JavaScript) client app that receives messages.</li> 
         </ol> 
         <p>You can send messages via the <a href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/admin/">Admin SDK</a> or the <a href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/server/">HTTP and XMPP APIs</a>. For testing or for sending marketing or engagement messages with powerful built-in targeting and analytics, you can also use the <a href="//console.firebase.google.com/project/_/notification/compose"> Notifications composer</a>.</p> 
        </div> 
        <h2 id="implementation_path">Implementation path</h2> 
        <table class="responsive implementation-path"> 
         <tbody>
          <tr> 
           <td><span class="numbered n1"></span></td> 
           <td>Set up the FCM SDK</td> 
           <td>Set up Firebase and FCM on your app according the setup instructions for your platform.</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td><span class="numbered n2"></span></td> 
           <td>Develop your client app</td> 
           <td>Add message handling, topic subscription logic, or other optional features to your client app. During the development, you can easily send test messages from the <a href="//console.firebase.google.com/project/_/notification/compose"> Notifications composer</a>.</td> 
          </tr> 
          <tr> 
           <td><span class="numbered n3"></span></td> 
           <td>Develop your app server</td> 
           <td>Decide whether you want to use the Admin SDK or one of the server protocols to create your sending logic  logic to authenticate, build send requests, handle responses, and so on. Then build out the logic in your trusted environment. Note that if you want to use upstream messaging from your client applications, you must use XMPP, and that Cloud Functions does not support the persistent connection required by XMPP.</td> 
          </tr> 
         </tbody>
        </table> 
        <h2 id="next_steps">Next steps</h2> 
        <ul> 
         <li> <p>Run the <a href="https://github.com/firebase/quickstart-android/tree/master/messaging">Android</a> or <a href="https://github.com/firebase/quickstart-ios/tree/master/messaging/">iOS</a> Quickstart sample. These samples let you run and review code to send a test message to a single device using the Firebase console.</p> </li> 
         <li> <p>Try the tutorials for <a href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/android/first-message">Android</a> or <a href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/ios/first-message">iOS</a>.</p> </li> 
         <li> <p>Add Firebase Cloud Messaging to your <a href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/android/client">Android</a>, <a href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/ios/client">iOS</a>, or <a href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/js/client">Web</a> app.</p> </li> 
         <li> <p>Set up your trusted environment. If you are writing your sending logic in Node.js, you can use the <a href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/admin/">Admin Node.js SDK's FCM API</a>, and readily deploy your code on Cloud Functions for Firebase. Alternatively, you can get help with server development using the raw protocols from the <a href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/server">server setup guide</a>, guides to <a href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/send-message">sending messages with your app server</a>, and the complete references for <a href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/http-server-ref">HTTP</a> and <a href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/xmpp-server-ref">XMPP</a>.</p> </li> 
         <li> <p>Learn more about sending data payloads, setting message priority, and other <a href="https://firebase.google.com/docs/cloud-messaging/concept-options">messaging options</a> that are available with FCM.</p> </li> 
         <li> <p>Migrate your existing <a href="http://developers.google.com/cloud-messaging/android/android-migrate-fcm">Android</a> or <a href="http://developers.google.com/cloud-messaging/ios/ios-migrate-fcm">iOS</a> GCM implementation to use Firebase Cloud Messaging.</p> </li> 
        </ul> 
       </div>
